ROAD NETORK ROVAE PROGRA )FVP
A. TE PROGRAM
1.         The economic development in Fujian Province has been shaped f%y its
geogrphic configurtion. The southern coastal corridor is generally much more developed
than the predominantly mountainous northern regions.  Lack of adequate road
infastucture is considered to be one of the major impediments to faster economic growth
in the influience areas of the existing roads.
2.          The Province has requested Bank financing to supplement its own resources
for the improvement of the network in the northern and northeastern part of the Province.
Most of the roads located in these regions have low geometic standards and poor surface
conditions. The RNIP component of the project includes seven subprojects tat are
geographically widespread, a deliberate step by the Province to promote improved project
preparation practices and technology transfer, normally assodated with the Bank's
involvement, to remote prefectures and counties. The rationale for selecting a particuar
road section for inclusion in the RNIP was deternined by the respective importance of the
road link in the network. Several of the road sections selected form part of the national
road network and also play an important role in the road transport needs of the prefectues
and counties concerned.
3.          The RNIP subprojects fall into two categories:
Group A: upgrading existing roads; 3 subprojects, 58.3 km;
Group B: paving existing gravel roads; 4 subprojects, 202.7 km.
B. ECONOMIC EVALUATION MErHODOILOGY FOR SUBPROnC'S
4.          RNIP subprojects were evaluated using a computer spreadset evaluation
model developed in previous Bank highway projects in Chira. The inputs to the model are
described in the following.
5.          Traffic Forecast. Fujian Province has experienced rapid economic growth
in recent years. As a result, highway taffic has been growing rapdly. Motor vehicle
regstation over the last 12 years grew at an annual average rate of 11.5 percent. Traffic
growth on the main areies of the network indicated a similar rate of growth. However,
historical records of traffic growth rates for motorized taffic (motor vehicles and tractors)
an the RNIP roads indicated an annual growth rate of between 4.8 and 6.5 percent over
the last seven-year period. Because of the hilly and mountainous nature of the terain, the



-94-                          A
volume of bicycle and animalArawn vehicle traffic was found to be insignificant on all
RNIP roads.
6.         It was assumed that traffic growth rates over a five-year period after the
improvement ( . the road conditions will be somewhat higher than indicated by the
historical trend, reflecting the expected increase in economic activity, with some tapering
off of the traffic during the following 10-year peiod. Additional taffic was assumed to
be generated by the improved condition of the roads at a rate of 10 percent of the nonnal
traffic.
7.          The estimated trffic volumes have been converted to an equivalent truck
traffic volume and compared witi the capacity of the road. The 4-ton medium truck
(5.5-ton GVW) was used as the standard vehicle, and all motorized traffic, including
tractors have been converted to medium-truck-equivalent (MTE) units, using a factor o
1.0. When the equivalent volume was lower than road capacity, the projected volume was
taken as the future traffic volume. When the projected traffic volume was highs than road
capacity, it was adjusted to be equal to the capacity of the road, and the volumes by
vehicle type were adjusted proportionately.
8.          Highway Capacity. The pracal capacity of a highway is defined as the
volume of trffic at the time when the stability of the traffic flow starts to break down.
Congestion effects, in the form of impedance of the faster vehicles by slower ones, will
be felt over the whole range of traffic volumes up to that volume, but instability of flow
and the onset of stop-and-go conditions will occur only after this volume is exceeded. The
practical capacity of a flat tangent 7-meter wide, two-lane highway is about 2,500
passenger car equivalent (pce) per hour. Since a medium-size truck is equivalent to 2
passenger cars, practical capacity for this type of highway is assumed to be 1,250 MTE
units per hour.
9.          Capacity is assumed to vary with the width of pavement. The following
adjustment factors were adopted to modify the capacity of a 7-meter wide road (with linear
interpolation) when the road width is different from 7 meters.
7.0 meters        1.00
6.7 meters        0.98
6.1 meters        0.90
5.5 meters        0.80
10.        Road capacity drops with increasing hilliness. The following factors were
adopted to modify capacity for each road geometric class:
Flat/Rolling:     0.85
Hilly:            0.65
Mountainous:      0.50



- 9S -                        ANM-
11.        Vehde Operating Costs. Vehicle operating costs were estimated in two
steps. First, free-flow operating costs were estimated and then the values were modified
to reflect the degree of traffic congestion. Free-flow operating costs for various types of
vehicle are listed in the detailed economic analysis for each of the RNIP roads in
Appendixes 2-8 to this Annex. To obtain an average operating cost for vehicle traffic, the
following fleet composition was assumed for motorized vehicle traffic on all roads
analyzed:
Vehicle type     Percentage
Small car               13
Small bus               13
Medium bus              4
Large bus               4
Small truck             16
Medium truck            33
Large truck             2
Tractr-Trailer          15
The average vehicle operating cost, weighted by the above percentage traffic composition,
were defined as follows:
Surface     Pavement    Flat/rolling   Hilly    Mountainous
Type                     Conditions
Paved         Good          0.73       0.88        1.02
Fair         0.81       0.98        1.11
Poor         1.01       1.16        1.30
Unpaved       Good          0.92       1.09       1.32
Fair         1.49       1.88        2.21
Poor         1.71       2.10        2.44
12.        The purchase price of mechanized, small tractor, widely used in China, was
estimated at about one sixth that of a small truck. Since the running cost is not considered
to be proportional to the purchase price, it was assumed that the operating cost of a tractor
is one fourth of the average vehicle operating cost of a small truck.
13.         Vehicle operating cost under congested conditions have been obtained by
multiplying free-flow-traffic operating cost wi-th a congestion factor, estimated as a function
of daily volume/capacity ratio. Congestion factors used for the different volume/capacity
ratios are listed as follows:



- 96 -                        ANEX I
Volume/Capacity
Ratio         .CongUo
0.0              1.00
0.6              1.00
0.7              1.05
0.8              1.15
0.9              1.5
1.0              2.5
14.        Road Mance Cost. The road maintenance cost is divided into fixed
and variable costs. The fixed cost is the expenses incurred when maintenance activities
are minimal and it does not change with the change in traffic volumes. In the evaluation,
the fixed cost was assumed to be Y 4,400 per Ian per year for roads with asphalt surface
and Y 4,700 per kn per year for gravel and earth roads. The varible cost changes with
changes in traffic volumes. It can be measured as a linear function of the daily traffic
volume. Values are Y 30.0 and Y 53.5 per vehicle per km per year for asphalt surface
and gravel surface roads, respectively. For example, the annual maintenance cost of a
gravel road with 200 vehicle per day would be:
4,700 + 53.5 x 200 = Y 15,400/lam.
C. DESCRlON OF SuBPROJEr
15.       TUngianguIa jiang Road (A-1). The Tingjiang-Lianjiang road is a section
of National Route No. 104, the main highway between Fuzhou and the eastemn part of the
Provn. The road passes through ftree townships and serves two countis with a total
area of 2,293 lmn2 and a population of 170,00. The area is rich in natural resources. The
local specialties are aquatic products, fruits and other agricultural and industrial products.
The Gross Value of Agriculture and Industry (GOVAI) reached Y 280 million in 1991.
16.        The existing road is 16.9 km long and characteized by high traffic volumes
and poor geometric standards. In 1992, Average Daily Traffic (ADT) reached 2,659
motorized vehicles. The road passes through densely populated towns such as Guangtou.
In particular, the Guangtou Mountain section of this road has very low geometric
standards. Sharp curves and steep graients are frequently encountered.
17.        The road would be upgraded to Class 2 standard, involving: (a) the
widening of the formation from 7-8 m to 12 m, and the pavement from 6-7 m to 7-8.5 m;
(b) building a new road section to bypass Guangtou Town; and (c) building a tunnel
(882 m) to bypass steep grades, which would shorten the travel distance near the northern
end of this section. The proposed project would greatly improve the conditions of the
exisdng road and reduce the length of the road by 2.8 km to 14.1 kms.
18.        xnkou-Dutouplng Road (A-2). The road is located in the suburb of
Sanming City, the third largest city of the Fujian Provirce. It serves as a vital link



-97 -                         AN       3
between Sanming City and its northwestern neighboring counties, such as Mingxi,
Jiaing, Taining and Jiangle. The influence of this road extends to areas rich in mineral
resources. The GOVAI in the region reached Y 5.1 billion in 1991.
19.        Starting at Jinxi, the alignment of the road is 9 km long with a maximum
gradient of 9 percent and a minimum curve radius of 13 m. There are 99 sharp curves
within this 9 km stretch. Moreover, it has an at-grade crossing of a railway marshalling
yard where vehicles aTe frequently delayed up to half an hour. In 1992, the ADT reached
1,453 motorized vehicles.
20.        The road would be realigned and upgraded to Class 3 standard with a
formation width of 8.5 m and a pavement width of 7.0 m. It would begin at XImkou
(about 4.6 km south of Jinxi), where it intersects National Route No. 205. The ro&d then
would cross the Sha River and folow the east bank of Huangsha Creek, and end at
Dutouping. A 400 m access road will also be built under this improvement scheme. Also,
the new alignment will eliminate a railway crossing and will be 3.5 kan shorter than the
existing alignment.
21.        Nakou-Shaowu Road (A-3). Nakou-Shaowu road (51.5 kIn) is located in
the northern industrial center of the Province in the Shaowu City region. The road's
mfluence area includes Shaowu City, Shunchang County and Nanping City with an area
of 4,812 knm2 lad population of 0.52 million. Besides various industrial products, the
agrcultural products of the region include rice, tea, timber and orange. The GOVAI of
the region reached Y 1.76 billion in 1991.
22.        The present Nakou-Shaowu road, located at the eastern bank of Futun River,
is a section of National Route No. 316. The road has very poor geometric stndards and
surface conditions. Sharp curves and steep grade are frequently encounteed. As a result,
vehicles can hardly pass during the rainy season. This is the only missing link, as an
engineered road, of National Route No. 316 in Fujian Provinze.
23.        The proposal is to build a Class 2 road on a new alignment between Nakou
and Shaowu city with 8.5 m wide formation and 7 m wide pavement in mountainous
ternin, and with 12 m wide formation and 9 m wide pavement through built up areas.
The road would begin at Nakou Town, run along the west bank of Futun River and
connect to Shaowu City through a recently completed bridge near the city center. The
road would bypass the difficult terrai of the east bank of the nver. The Province is also
plaming to upgrade the Nakou-Dagan road, the immediate southern section of National
Route No. 316, to the same standard as the Nakou-Shaowu road. Once completed, the
road will provide a direct route for the north-south corridor taffic between the Province's
northern, underdeveloped region and the southern, coastal gion.
24.        At present, most of the traffic between Shaowu and Naping travel via Jianou
over a distance of 203 kn. In 1992, ADT traffic between Shaowu and Nakou reached
1,252 motorized vehicles. The new road will shorten the distance between Shaowu and
Nakou by 12.7 km.



- 98 -                        ANNEX 3
25.        Gutian-Zhenqha Road (B-i). Gutian-Zhenqian Road is located in the
northeastem hinterland ei Fujian Province and forms part of the An-Song highway,
connecting Zhejiang and Fujian provinces. The road's influence area mainly covers
Pingnan County. It provides service to 10 towns and 211 villages with a population of
0.76 million. The major industrial and agricultural products in the regions include paper,
chemicals, raw materials, wine, tea, timber, etc. In 1991, the GOVAI reached Y 950
1nillion in the region.
26.        The gravel-surfaced Class 4 road (101.3 kIn) has a formation width of 6-8
m and a pavement width of 5-6 m. As the traffic volume increases, it is getting more and
more difficult to maintain the road. Moreover, the road becomes muddy dunng the raining
season and dusty during the dry season. In 1992, the ADT reached 558 motorized
vehicles. The proposed improvement is to pave the entire length of the road with asphalt-
penetration macadam.
27.        Huhtugban-Shouning Road (B-2).  The Hutangban-Shouning road
(47.5 kIn) is located in the northeastern mountainous regiom of the Province. It is a section
of the provincial area highway that connects Zhejiang Province and Shouning and Fuan
counties. The road links Shouning Town of Shouning County with Hutangban Town of
Fuan County. The road's influence area extends to 3,153 km2 with a population of 0.75
million. The major products of the region include tmber, bamboo, tea and Chinese
medicine. In 1991, the GOVAI in the region reached Y 1 billion.
28.        The existing road is a gravel-surfaced Class 4 road. Its formation width
varies between 6 to 10 m and its pavement width between 5.5 and 6.0 m. The ADT in
1992 reached 429 motoized vehicles. The proposed improvement is to pave the existing
road with an asphalt macadam surface and to widen the road's formation to a minimum
of 7.5 m, and the pavement to 6 m.
29.        Zhouaing-Zheuqian Road (3-3). Zhouning-Zhenqian road (26.9 kin) is
also located in the northeasrn region of the Province. It links Daqiao Town of Zhouning
County and Zhenqian Town of Zhenhe County. The area of influence of the road extends
to 733 villages with a population of 0.89 million. The major products of the region
include bamboo, timber, tea and other agricultural products. In 1991,  the GOVAI of the
region reached Y 1.2 billion.
30.        The exisdng gravel-surfaced road is 7.5 m to 8.5 m wide. In 1992, the
ADT reached 512 motorized vehicles. The proposed improvement is to surface the road
with asphalt-peneation macadam. Once completed, the road will be the first road with
a paved surface in Zhouning County.
31.         etlan-Donshanqiao Road.  Hetian-Dongshanqiao road (27.0 kIn) is
located in the northwest region of the Province in Changtin County, near tie border
between Fujian and Jiangxi provinces. The area where the road is located is rich in
forestry reserves. The 27 km long road serves 19 vilages with population of about
130,000. In 1991, GOVAI in die region reached Y 97 million. In 1992, the ADT reached



-99 -                           NN    3
525 vehicles per dpy. The proposed improvement is to surface the gravel road with
awphalt-penetration macadam; formation width-7.5 m, pavement width-6.0 m.
32.         A summary of the economic evaluation and the estimated economic costs of
the RNIP subprojects are provided in Appendix 1 to this Annex. The details of the
economic evaluation for each of the RNIP subprojects are presented in Appendixes 2 to
8 to this Annex.
D. ORGANIZATONAL ARRANGEMENTS FOR TME EXECUTMON OF RNIP
33.         The Fujian Provincial Highway Administration Bureau wouid be the
executing agency for the RNIP at the provincial level. An RNIP Unit within FPHAB has
been set up for the overall management and coordination of the preparation and
implementation of the RNIP. The Unit is headed by a Deputy Director and includes two
highway planners, two financial administrators and three technical personnel. Similarly
setctured units have been established in Futhou and Sanming municipalities and Nanping,
Ningde and Longyan districts where the roads included in the RNIP are located.
34.         The RNIP Unit within FPHAB has the responsibility for (a) engineering
design, economic evaluation, preparation of th, bidding documents and technical
specifications, the execution of the procurement process and signing construction contracts
in the preparation phase of the Program; and (b) overall planning, financial administration,
saf trafiing and the setting up or strengthening field laboratories during the
implementation phase of the Program. The RNIP units at mumicipal and prefecture level
have responsibility for (i) land acquisition, relocation, resettlement and environmental
protection activities; (ii) organization and supervision of construction; and (iii) regular
monitoring and reporting of implementation progress.
35.         The construction supervision orgnzation for the RNIP has also been
determined. It is a hree-level strucure comprising (a) the Chief Supervision Engineer of
the Fujian Provincial Supaevision Departnent who will be the Engineer in tenns of the
general conditions of the construction contacts; (b) the Office of the Engineer's
Representative who will act on behalf of the Engineer as authorized; and (c) the offices of
the Resident Engineers for each of the seven contra  who will be responsible for on-site
supervision. The staff of the Fujian Highway Consulting Engineers Inc. would be involved
in the suprvision, supporting local personnel of the transport bureaus at the prefecture and
county levels. The responsibilities at all three levels of the organization struchtre have
been well defined. On the level of the Resident Engineers, abon't 40 supervision personnel
will be involved in field supervision of the seven subprojects.

- 108-                        ANNE
HIGHWAY CONSTRUCTION lUSTRY
Provincial Road Construction Industry Study and
Nationwide Survey
A. INRODUCTION
1.         The Bank has had a long-standing interest in the further development of the
construction industry in China. During 1988 and 1989, the Bank, with the assistance of
sever line ministries of the cental government, carried out a brief study of the status of
the industry. The study identified the major opeaonal deficiencies that provided the basis
for the formulation of a tentative progam for the industry's furither development. Because
of the slowdown and changed priorities of the Bank's involvement in China during
1989-91, it was only in the latter part of 1992 that the study was followed up with
technical assistance (TA) to the Ministry of Construction under the Bank's TOC credit
facility.
2.         Also, with the accelerated development of the road network in China and
the Bank's continued support for the subsector, the Bank's attention has been focused more
and more on the development needs of the highway construction industry. The Bank's
lending for highway projects has exceeded $1.0 billion, representing about one third of the
close to $3.0 billion cost of highway construction works involved. The Bank, in the
course of project supervision, had the opportunity to gain a better understanding of the
operational characteristics of the highway construction units participang in the
implementation of Bank-financed projects.
3.         On the basis of such expeience and as an outcome of the Bank's regular
exchange of views with the representaives of the central government, a consensus has been
reached that the highway construction industry would require urgent reinforcement and
modenization to overcome its major deficiencies. In particular, it was recognized that the
industry's present technical and financial resources and limited experience in the
construction of high-standard highways would not be adequate to meet the challenge posed
by GOC's ambitious medium- and long-term progrms for the rebuilding of the
interprovincial highway network to meet the r idly increasing road transport demand. As
a step in this direction, an understanding has t i reached with the centrl government and
Fujian Province that the proposed Fujian Provincial Highway Project would include a study
of the provincial road construction industry.
4.         In support of the execution of such a study, and to pursue a broader
nationwide svey of the industry's profile, the Bank requested a TA grant under the



-109 -                        ANNEX 4
Japanese Policy and Human Resource Development Funds from the Japanese Govemment
in November 1992. Funds of X 43.8 milion (about $400,000 equivalent) were granted in
early 1993, providing TA for:
(a)   a study of the Fujian provincial road construction industry for the
(i) assessment of the capabilities of the provincial road construction
industry, (ii) identification of existing problems in road construction and
possible solutions, and (iii) recommendations for reforms, as appropriate,
in the interest of improving the operational environment for the provincial
road construction enterprises;
(b)   a survey and its analysis relating to the (i) assessment of the capacity and
efficiency of highway construction industry enterprises in China,
(ii) identification of development needs of the enterprises, and
(iii) recommendations for appropriate measures required in the policy and
regulatory framework for more efficient operation of the industry.
5.         The study, indicated in para. 4(a), would be carried out in the framework
of the proposed Fujian Provincial Highway Project. The foreign exchange cost of the
study, primarily for the services of foreign consultants, will financed in part from the TA
provided under the Japanese Grant ($180,000) and in part from the proceeds of the Bank
loan ($150,000). Services, facilities, equipment and counterpart personnel for the study
will be provided by the Fujian Government.
6.         The nationwide highway construction industry survey and follow-up analysis
referred to in para. 4(b) will be carried out as a separate exercise by a joint local/foreign
team. The foreign exchange cost of the survey will be financed from the remaining
$220,000 of the Japanese Grant. The survey will be coordinated by the Ministry of
Communications (MOC) with services, facilities and counterpart personnel for the survey
to be provided by the central government.
7.         In the following, this annex provides an outline TOR for the Fujian
Provincial Road Constructon Industry Study (PRCIS) and an outlne TOR for the
Nationwide Highway Construction Industry Survey.
B. OthINE Tom  oF REFE   FoR
TE FWuAN PROviNCiAL RoAD CONSunoN INSTY STUDY
General
1.         The Fujian Provincial Transport Departnent (FPTD) intends to wudeke
a study of the highway construction industry and develop a plan of action for the
strengthening of the construction industry and improving its operating environment to
foster the growth, qualiq and stabihty of the industry.



- 110-                        ASN=  4
2.         To accomplish the study, a consultant firm will be retained to work with
personnel of the Fujian Government and local professional and supporting staff.
3.         The study will comprise the survey of market demand and the identification
of the deficiencies of the industry, and the constraints of the operating environment
affecting the operation of the of the provincial road construction enterprises. The study
will lead to the preparation of an action plan for implementing its recommendatioils.
Study Objectives
4.          The study has three main objectives:
(a)   To compare the highway construction market demand for the next 10 yean
to the capabilities of the industry, and identify the deficiencies and the
requirements of the industry to meet such demand.
(b)   To study the intemnal and extemal constraints of the contractors that impede
their operation, and make recommendations for the necessary measures for
improvements.
(c)   To develop an action plan that, if implemented, would lead to an increase
in the capacity and efficiency of the provincial highway consucton
industry.
Key Isues
5.         The study team will identify key issues that should be addressed and studied
during the course of the study. It is expected that the following will be among the key
issues:
(a) The capacity of the industry in relatioAn to the expectd investment program
for road works in the Province.
(b)   The means of technology transfer to and intemal restructuring of the
construction enterpises to increase the efficiency of operations and improve
the quality of works.
(c) The options for channeling financial assistance to the construction
enterprises to meet investment needs and loan repayment conditions.
(d)   The impact of the reform meaes on the industry's opeation.
(e)   The enhancement of motivation and competitive spirit of the crporaons
in the line with the objecdves of a socialist market economy.
(f)   The identification of alternative modes of financing road investments.



- 1ll -                                4
(g)   The presentation of an action plan for implementing the study's
recommendations.
Scope of Work-Principal Areas of Activities
6.          Five principal areas of work, as well as work tasks for each area, have been
identified as follows:
AREA A:   Quantify the market demand for the next 10 years
Task A.l:   Determine the profile of FPID's road construction and
mantenance program.
Task A.2:   Determine the market demand of other entities such as
prefectures and municipalities.
Task A.3:   Determine the amount of road construction and maintenance
works to be done by direct labor, if any, by the various
transport departments.
AREA B:   Determine an Industry profile to meet the projected highway
market
Task B.  I Determine the capacity required in terms of class of roads
involved, major construction items, and the type of prefer
supply, i.e., whether by specialized or general construcon
enterprises.
Task B.2    Determine the opfimal size, the number and prefered
geographical distribution of constrution enterprises.
Task B.3    Study the viability, profitability and oganization of the
industry, and consider the merits of the establishmet of a
representative body for fte industry.
AREA C:   Identify the Industry deficies and the measu   needed to
achieve a desirable Industry profile
Task C.1    Detmine capacity in terms of manpower, equipment and
financial resources.
Task C.2    Compare existing industry capacity to prqjected demand.
Task C.3   Identify and classify capacity shortfalls.



- 112 -                        ANNEX4
Task C.4    Analyze options for meeting shortfalls in construction
capacity through strengthening and expanding existing
construction enterprises, increasing the number of
enterprises, using contractors from outside the province,
facilitating the setting up of foreign/local joint ventures, and
attracfing private financing through BOT or other means.
Task C.5    For the strengthening and expanding of the provincial
construction enterprises:
(a)  identify equipment requirements, ways of financing
equipment purchase and alternative means of access to
equipment, such as leasing;
(b)  identify the areas for institutional strengthening, such
as organizational structure, operational and financial
management practices, manpower requirements,
including training needs, and define the means for
addressing identified deficiencies;
(c)   recommend  measures  for  operational  and
technological improvements in order to increase
productivity, efficiency, and improve quality.
AREA D:   Identify adverse Industry environmental constraints
Task D. 1    Study existing operating environment.
Task D.2    Study government policies that may impact on the
contractors' profitability, productivity, and efficiency.
Task D.3    Study the reform  measures being introduced for the
transformation of state-owned industrial enterprises and
analyze the impact of such measures on the highway
construction industry.
Task D.4    Study the policy of price controls and "quota system" and
determine their impact on the industry.
Task D.5    Study possible remedies to limited profits and social burdens
affecting the enterprises.
Task D.6   Study the construcion matrial supply system, pricing and
availability, and look into the viability of establihsing
enterprises for the supply of key construction materials of
controlled quality.



- 113-                         AN 4
AREA E:   Identify practices of employers that Impact the growth,
producti;ity, and efficiency of the construction Industry
Task E. 1    Study the preconstruction process in FPTD  and other
government units at prefecture, municipality and county
levels.
Task E.2    Study prequalification, bidding and contracting practices.
Task E.3    Study contract administration practices.
Implementation
Organization
7.          The PRCIS would be carried out by a Study Team under the guidance of a
high-level Steering Comnittee and a Technical Coordination Group.
8.          Because of the diverse and complex nature of the study, the Study Team
would comprise local technical personnel well acquainted with provincial conditions
influencing the operation of the road construction enterprises and foreign eoosultants with
broad international experience in construction industry management and operatons.
9.          The core personnel of local study team has been identified comprsing tre
technical staff from FTI and one each from the Fujian Traffic Institute and the Science
and Technology Advisory Center, Traffic Transportation Society. The full-time services
of the personnel identified would extend over the 10-month duration of the study,
representing 50 staff-months of input. Additional personnel would be ,i.obilized as
required with an estimated 10 staff-months of input.
10.        It is estimated that the execution of the study would require an input of about
9 staff-months of foreign consultant serices involving 4-5 experts having experience
primarily in the following disciplines: (a) management and operation of highway
construction enterprises; (b) commercialization and corporatization of the highway
construction industry; (c) highway construction equipment utilizaton, maintenance and
leasing; (d) highway construction and contract management-related staff training; and (e)
policies, regulations and procedures relevant to the operation of enterises in a market-
oriented environment.
11.         Consultants would be selected from a shortlist of experienced intemational
consulting firms following Bank procedures. In the selection of the firms, much
importance will be attached to the relevant qualifications and experience of the members
of the proposed consulting team.

the Leading Group for the implementation of the Fuzhou-Xiamen-Zhangzhou Expressway
as follows:

Deputy Director of the Provincial Transport Departnent
Deputy Director of the Provincial Construction Commission
Deputy Secretary General of the Provincial Govemment
13.        The role of the Steering Committee would be to provide guidance to the
Study Team on major policy issues. It is envisaged that the Steering Committee would
meet to discuss the findings and recommendations of the reports released at the various
stages of the study. Other provincial government departments and central govenment
ministries would be consulted by the Steering Committee as considered appropiate.
14.        The Techincal Coordination Group would comprise the representatives of
pwvincial govemment departments, provincial institutions, road constructon enterprises,
and from time to time, technical personnel of the central govemnment and representatives
of the World Bank. More specifically, the Technical Coordination Group would include
the representatives of the following provincial entities:
Structural Reform Committee
Department of Finance
Construction Committee
FPTD-Highway Administration Bureau
Road Construction Enterprises (including rresentatives of larger, medium-
size and small enterprises)
Technical personnel from other departments and institutions are expected to be invited to
participate in the Group's functions as considered appropriate.
15.        The Technical Coordination Group would provide technical advice and
guidance to the Study Team and assist coordination with local institutions in the inteest
of expediting information and data transfer to the Study Team. It is envisaged that the
Technical Coordination Group would meet as fiequently as required for providing adequate
and timely support to the Study Team.
Execution of the Study and Reporting
16.        The study would be executed in three phases over a period of about
10 months. The first phase (about two months) would be devoted to detailed definition of
the study's program, identification of the key sources of information and initiation of data
collecdon. At the end of the first phase an Inception Report would be issued. During the
second phase of the study (about six months), an in-depth analysis of the information and
iniial consolidation of the findings would be undeaken, leading to the preparation of a



- 115- A-r
Draf FiYnal Report. During this phase, an about one-month study tour, with the
partipation of about 10 members of the Chinese team involved in the study, would be
organized to neighboring developing and developed countries to make contact with road
construction enterprises and related instituttons. During the third phase of the study (about
two months) the conclusions, recommendations and plans for follow-up actions would be
formulated and consolidated in the FYnal Report.

lle Survey

Executo and Management
2.         The Executing Agency for the survey would be the Ministry of
Communications. The survey would be executed by a Survey Team comprising a joint

Execution of the Survey
3.         The Survey Team would comprise local technical personnel familiar with the

data for futue monitoring.

E,NVMINRqTA ASE$M$ffA
ACTON PLAN SU$YR
A. BACKGROUND
1.         During September 1991, the Fujian Provincial Environmental Protection
Research insttute (FPEPRI) conducted an envinmental assessment of fte proposed
highway, with the participation of the Highway Science Research Institute of MOC.
Environmental monitoring and field surveys were carried out by local environmental units
between September 1991 and July 1992. The State Environmental Proction Bureau
(SEPB) approved the outine for this environmental assessment in February 1992, and the
Eironmental Impact Statement (EIS) of the Quanhou-Xiamen Expressway Secton of
Fuzhou-Xlamen Highway was submitted to MOC and SEPB in August 1992. The process
of environmental review involved inputs from various units throughout the Province,
inciuding provincial environmental bureaus, research institutes, and universities.
2.          The policy and administrative requirements for environmental assessmnent of
development projects in China were followed during preparation and evaluation of this EA.
Applicable laws and regulations for this EA include:
(a)   Environmental Procion Law of PRC;
(b)   Atmospheric Pollution Abatement Law of PRC;
(c)   Water Pollution Abatement Law of PRC;
(d)   Management Guidelines on Environmental Protection of Construction
Projects, Number 003 (86), issued by SEPB;
(e)   Measures for Environmental Protection Management of Trnsport
Construction Projects, Number 117 (86), issued by the Ministry of Urban
and Rural Construction and Environmental Protection; and
(i)   Measur   for Environmental Protection  Management of Transport
Constructon Projects, Number 17, issued by MOC.
3.          The environmental standards applied in the assessment and specific standards
and critria applied for air quality, noise, vibration, and surface water are listed in
Appendix 1 to this annex.



-119 -                        A X  5
B. ENRoNm TAL AwSS MT, XwAME-QuANZOU HGHwAY
4.         The road lengths included in the environmental assessment of the highway
were the Xiamen-Quanzhou Highway (81.4 Ian), the link road to Jimei (Xiamen) (6.2 km),
and the link road to Shedian in Jinjiang County (6.3 km). The environmental assessment
covered an area 500 m from each side of the central line of the highway for atmospheric
impacts, and a belt area of up to 500 m from each shoulder of the highway for noise and
vibration impacts. A summary of the criteria applied for environmental evaluation is
presented in Appendix 2.
Characteristics of the Highway Corridor
5.         Topography and Climate.  The alignment of the Xiamen-Quanzhou
Highway passes through an area characterzed by a terain that is higher in the south and
west, with a gentle, average grade of 0.02 percent from west to east. The plain is densely
interwoven with a network of rivers and canals. The annual average temperature is about
21 C. The region lies in a subtropical monsoon zone and is occasionally hit by typhoons
and heavy rainstorms, with annual rainfall ranging between 1,090 and 1,478 mm, mostly
concetrated between May and September.
6.         Population. The Xiamen-Quanzhou section of the highway comprises an
influence area of about 5,700 km2, with a population of over 5 million and an average
population density of 920 people per kn2. The area along the alignment of the highway
has a ppulation of about 66,000, thousand, comprising the 98 natural villages within a
250-m range of the road. The cultivated area is 40,700 mu, about half of which is
irted.
7.         Agriculture. The region along the proposed highway route represents an
important rice- and fruit-growing area in southern Fujian. In the past, agriculture was
dominant in economic activity in this corndor. However, the recent rapid growth of
township enterprises has allowed industry to also contribue significantly to GOVAI in the
Province. Based on a 1991 survey of 64 villages along the highway, industrial activities
contributed 64 percent and agriculture 36 percent of GOVAI. Among the agricultural
activities, farming accounted for 74 percent of output value, followed by animal husbandry
(12 percent), fisheries (7 percent), and forestry (0.7 percent), with the remainder
(6.3 percent) in other agricultural activities. There is significant variance in the dominance
of agriculura areas in various parts of the Province. Sections of Tong'an Country, Jimai,
and Xinglin near the Xiamen Special Economic Zone, and Jinjiang County, and Licheng
Disrict. The major agricultural products are grain, sugarcane, peanuts, fruit, and
freshwater cultivadon. Economic activity in agriculture varies along sections of the route
due to notable differences in terrain, soil, and water supply.
8.         Cu u       oraH   Locations. There are numerous cultural, histonc, and
scenic spots within and near Xiamen and Quanzhou, to which the proposed highway would
increase access. Major attracions include Gulangyu Island, Riguangyan, Zhongshan Park,
Nanputuo Temple, and Aoyuan Garden in the vicinity of Xiamen. Sites in Quanzhou



- 120 -                        ANNX S
include Zingjin Temple, Kaiyuan Ancient Temple, and Mt. Qingyuan. The Tongmin'an
Pass on Mt. Xiaoyingling is also located along the route, but will not be directly affected
by the highway alignment (para. 17).
9.          Noise and Vibration. Existing noise quality in the villages along the route
is satisfactory. Noise levels were measured based on various samples taken along seven
sections of the route. Noise was monitored for 24 hours at three locations on the Fuzhou-
Xiamen Highway, one location on the Quanzhou-Xiutu Highway, one location on the
Quanzhou-Jinjiang Highway, one location in the Jinjiang-Anhui Highway, and one location
on the Xiamen-Zhangzhou Highway. Based on results collected at 26 specific sites, noise
levels average 56 dB(A) during the day and 49 dB(a) at night. Noise levels at night
exceeded state standards in three of the sites surveyed.
10.        Air Quality. Ambient air quality was monitored at nine points along the
Xiamen-Quanzhou section, including villages, areas of access to expressway interchanges,
industrial zones, and scenic areas. The baseline monitoring program included analysis of
NO,, CO, THC, Pb and TSP (total suspended particulates) during a five-day periel in the
summer season. Results conforned with state standards, and, where classified standards
exist, results met Class 1 standards.
11.        Water Quality. Water quality was assessed based on sampling of six
sections along the main waterways that the highway would cross (the Jinjiang, Xixi, and
Jiuxi Rivers and the Nanxi Canal). Sampling and analysis was carried out in accordance
with national guidelines. The monitoring program included pH, SS, permanganate
indexes, BOD5, oils, and lead. Samples results ranged between Class I and Im standard
at most sites. However, the water quality at two specific sections located in Nanqu
Chennel and Xixi River reached Class IV standard: the main contributing factors in this
case were domestic sewage and rain, which increased the level of organic matter and oils.
Potenthl Environmental Impact Identified In EA
12.        The following key areas of environmental impact were identified, where
adverse changes may take place during the construction and operation of the new highway:
(a)   Social disruption would directly affect an estimated 15,500 individuals who
will be resettled or compensated for severance (Annex 6). The construction
of an access-controlled highway will also disrupt communication between
communities and mobility between residential and farming areas.
(b)   Air pollution could be caused by dust generated during construction,
primarily by earthmoving machinery and trucks and also by stockpiled
materials at depots and quarries. The operation of the asphalt plants and
construction traffic could produce excessive noxious fumes. At the
oqEkrAtion phase, there could also be some localized concentration of S02 or
NO, during hours of peak traffic and under certain weather conditions along
the highway.



- 121 -                        A       5
(c)   Water polution could occur during construction from excessive spillage of
earth and other building materials, such as lime and fly-ash, into irrigation
channels and waterways. During construction and operon of the highway,
there is also a potential for water conamination from oil and fuel leaks from
gas stations and fuel depots where surface waters run close to such spots.
The effect of heavy rain following penods of drought could increase COD
concentration for a period of a few hours.
(d)   Noise and vibration levels could become excessive from the operation of
plants and machinery, as well as from normal traffic after the opening of the
highway wherever the new highway alignment will be close to villages.
During construction, noise from construction plants, cutting, quarrying, and
blasting will influence an area 200 m from the given site. During operation,
noise levels along the route are ewected to rise along with traffic volume,
and at night could exceed state standards as early as the year 2000. Two
sensitive sections of the route have been identified as equiring mitigatng
measures against excessive noise levels during the first stage of highway
construction.
(e)   Soil erosion could lead to a potential loss of hundreds of tons of topsoil per
year from exposed slopes of cuts and embankments of the highway and
borrow pits, particularly during penods of heavy rain. Six sections along
the route, which involve significant exposure of soil slope after cutting, have
been classified as erosion-sensitive. An additional 22 filling sections are
considered erosion-sensitive.
(f)   Soil pollution could result from lead emitted by motor vehicles, and after
accumulation, could affect crops grown along the highway. The influence
area of this damage will be 100 m and the lead content in soil could reach
76 mg/kg. According to some data projected during the ETA process, when
daily traffic volurzie exceeds 20,000 vehicles per day, the lead content in the
soil could be at least 10 times the baseline value. Based on current
esimates, lead content in soil may reach serious levels after several decades
of highway operation.
Measum for Monitoring and Mitigating Environmental [mpacts
13.        Social Disruption. The highway route was selected from among three
altives, with a view to avoid environmentally sensitive areas and to minimize negative
impacts on the local population, including the need for resettlement and land acquisition.
in  der to maintain or restore communication along the proposed highway, 39 grade
separtions, 167 underpasses and 6 interchanges are included along the route. These
feures will allow the affected population to remain mobile between residental and work
or farm areas, and will improve access to the new highway from major populadon centers.



- 122 -                       ANNEKS
14.        Air Qualty. Periodic monitoring of the atmosphere will be carried out to
deal with waste gases emitted from asphalt-mixig plants, dust from construction, key
sensitive areas, and areas in which complaints are made by residents. During the opeaon
phase of the highway, routine air monitoring will be carried out. Five monitoring points
would be set up along the highway to monito CO in the air, and NO;, TSP, and Pb in the
dust. Monitoring will be carried out during four, five-day monitoring periods each year,
with collection of four to five samples per day in fair-weather conditions. Management
of bulk materials and dust cargoes will be strengthened and piling in open air minimized.
Goods will be stored in dry places at least 500 m from the villages on the lee of wind
direction. Construction sites, access roads, and borrow areas will be frequently wateed
to reduce dust.
15.        Control of Noise and Vibration. Monitonng of vibration and noise will
be conducted twice a year for the villages within 100 m of the road. Such monitoring will
either be carred out twice daily, in the morning and the evening, or will be on a
continuous (automatic) basis. While at present noise levels are not excessive, they are
expected to dramatically increase by the year 2015. The use of noise-proof shelter belts
is planned, consisting of evergreen trees. The Province has zoning regulations in place to
restrict the development of new housing or schools within 100 m on either side of the
highway. During construction, noise impacts will be controlled by confining construction
activities to the hours between 6:00 and 22:00. Unnecessary noise from hauling, blasting
and other construction activities will be controlW and minimized. Hours of operation of
constuction plans will also be modified to reduce excessive noise. During operation, noise
will be monitored monthly to ensure that, within a 70 m radius from the central line of the
highway, noise does not surpass 77 dB(A). During the first phase of highway
construction, sound barriers will be erected along 12 sensitive sections of the route. Two
acoustic barriers (totaling 600 m) will also be eected, at Dongxin (10M 4.7) and Gouwei
(KM 34.3).
16.        Water Management. Monitoring will be carried out monthly in areas of
soil erosion, especially the river course down Jiasha Large Bridge, until the completion of
construction. The main items monitored are oils, COD, and suspended solids (silt).
During the operation phase, water will be monitored in eight key river sections and at the
oudet of the sewer system in Puli service area. The monitoring exercise will be carried
out semiannually-during the high-water period (May to June) and during the drought
period (December to January). At key river reaches, such as the lower reaches of Jiasha
Large Bridge and Puli service area, monitoring will take place monthly. This program will
involve monitoring of pH, oils, SS, COD,,, BOD5, Pb, and permanganate index. An
independent drainage system will be used to prevent rain wash from being directly
discharged into the waters to affect aquaculture and crops. Monitonng points will be
established for periodic analysis of water samples.
17.        Cultural/Historic Locations. It was originaly expected that a small number
of cultural sites, including the Tongming'an Pass, would be dircdy affected by
constuction of the highway. However, subsequent changes in the alignment have resulted
in a route that avoids these cultural sites altogether. While there are no known sites with



- 123 -
cultura or historic relics along the route, contractors would be required to stop work in
case relics are discovered during construction, and to seek guidance from an Antiquities
Presvation Agency in the Province.
18.        Sogl Pollton. The lead content in soil, rice, and vegetables will be
monitored once a year in the relevant areas, in Cidian, Tong'an County, and Jinjiang
County. Samples will be taken when rice and fruit are ripe, in addition to soil cores of
the topsoil. To mitigate the negative impact of lead on soil and cp, within a range of
100 m from the road, economic plants will be cultivated instead of grain or vegetables.
19.        Other. The project includes forestation in designated zones, which would
provide protection against pollution and would preserve the ecological environment. An
area 20 m wide would be reserved on both sides of the road for forestaion, which in total
would comprise at least 30 percent of the land area required for highway constuction.
Areas 20 m wide should be kept in advance to establish greenbelts in farmland areas that
would protect against lead pollution. In residential areas, 20 to 30 m wide spaces should
be reserved. In addition, 25 percent of the area around interchanges and 5 to 10 percent
(or at least 40 m) of the area at filling stations should be afforested.
C. ENVIRONNENTAL ASS          r FOR TME ROAD NETWORK
IMROVEMENT P}ROGRAM
20.        The route for the RNIP was chosen from considered altematives to minimize
the acquisition of land, impact on residential areas and historical sites, and to avoid
sensitive environmental feaures.
21.         In group A subprojects, rainstorm and flood risks have been taken into
consideration ir the design of bridges. Te resulting design was according to flood
frequency of once per 100 years for large bridges, and one per 50 years for medium and
small bridges as well as roadbeds and culverts. Measures to mitigate soil erosion include
planting vegetation to protect side slopes.
22.         The group A subprojects will also cause socua disruption, including the
resettlement of approximately 700 people. Details of the resettement and compensation
procedures to be followed are provided in Annex .
23.         Noise and air pollution have also been addressed in the environmental
measures proposed for the RNIP. The resurfacing of roads included in the RNIP
subpojects would reduce noise and air pollution. Extra protection would be provided by
planting groves of trees, 15-20 m wide and 270 m long, on both sides of the road. Extra
protection would be provided in sensitive areas as needed.
D. ENVONMENTAL ACtON PL SN
24.         The EAP summary stipulates how the environmental impacts idenified in
the EA are going to be dealt with at the design, implementation and opeaton phases of



- 124 -                       ANNEX5
the highway, and what administrative arrangements have been made for the execution of
the EAP during the three distinct phases of the development of the project. Appendices
3 and 4 summarize the key environmental issues to be addressed for the highway as well
as the RNIP.
E. ORGA1NIONAL ARRNGEMENTS AND MoNITRNG
25.        FPECDO, administrating agency for construction of the proposed highway,
has overall responsibility for coordinating environmental activities associated with the
project. FPECDO is directly responsible for executing the policies and laws of the State
and MOC in the project context, including preparation of the EAP and technical work
related to the environment. Supervision and monitoring activities of FPECDO include
monitoring construction works carried out on its behalf, identification and treatment of
pollution sources and handling of contamination accidents, maintenance of environmental
monitoring stations in cities and counties along the route to conduct periodic obseaions,
establishment of technical files on environmental protection, and supervision and inspection
asocated with implementation of the EAP during the operation phase.
26.        The Fujian Provincial Environmental Protection Bureau (FPEPB) will
exercise unified supervision and management of environmental requirements under its
jurisdiction, with input at all stages of the project. In conjunction with local environmental
protection units, FPEPB will provide assistance to FPECDO to carry out environmental
management, on- and off-site. Under FPEPB, environmental monitoring and management
will be canied out by environmental protecdon bureaus in the municipalities of Quanzhou
and Xamen, and by environmental protection departments in counties, cities, and districts
along the route. According to the EAP, monitoring of ongoing construction works and
implementation of the EAP will be coordinated by a designated individual within each
construction unit.
27.        The implementation and monitoring of environmental aspects of the RNIP
has involved various organizations at different stages in the project process. The definition
of environmental measures to be taken during the design phase was carried out by units
of EPHAB and researh and design in the localities of the RNIP subprojects.
Environmental measures will be the responsibility of the contractor during the construction
stage. Monitonng of the EAP will be achieved through units of FPEPB and FPHAB in
the subprtoject areas, comprising Fuzhou, Sanming, Shaowu, Ningde, and Longyan. This
organization will permit on-site monitonng of EAP progress.
28.        Training in environmental protection would be provided by the Province for
environmental administrators and other staff for both the highway and the RNIP. The
training program, which includes both domestic and overseas training, covers relevant
management and technical subjects in the environmental field.

- 137 -                       ANNEX.6
IRESETILEMA   ACTION PLAN S
A. POUCY BASS OF LAND ACQUISITON AND RESmwQ
1.         The Land Administration Law of China and the Fujian Provincial Land
Administration Regulations provide the legal basis for land acquisition and resettlement to
be undertakn in connecton with the construction of highways. In addition, to initiate
action on land acquisition and resettlement for major highway projects, SPC's approval of
the feasibility study recommendations and MOC's approval of the preliminary engineering
design are required.
B. COMP ASION POUCIES
2.          According to provincial regulations, the land acquisition process must
include compensation for land and young crops, plus a resettlement subsidy. The
following compensation provisions apply:
(a)   Crop Compensation = 1/2 x annual production value of acquired land
(b)   Land Compensation = 5 x the annual production value of acquired land
(c)   Resettlenent subsidy = 2 x annual production value of acquired land x
agiculture population + total acquired land.
3.          Compensation fees for crops and properes on the land acquired will be paid
directdy to original land users and owners. Compensation for borrowed land will also be
paid to landowners, at an annual rate of 10 percent of the compensation that would apply
for land acquisition.
4.          Contract prices include compensation for land acquisition, the temporary
occupation (borrowing) of land, and lesettlement. Forms of compensation that are not paid
directy to individuals and collective units, such as the cost of rebuilding public facilities
and resettling laborers, will be provided for in a development fund maintained at local
levels. The funds received by local agencies will be used for the fuiher development of
township enterprises, to provide employment opportunities for dislocated workers and
subsistence allowances for individuals who are unable to work. In addition, a portion of
the funds will be reserved for the establishment of village enterprises, development of
aquaculture, construction of small industrial estates, reclamation of wasteland, and
improvement of low-yielding farmland.



- 138 -                       ANNEX
5.          According to provincial regulations, certain local taxes and other financial
obligations to government are exempted: for example, agncultural tax, farmland
occupation tax, and the requirement to sell grain to the government would be parially or
wholly relieved. Such forms of compensation are included in the contracts made for
resettlement, and typically managed by public authorities.
6.         Compensation for buildings is based on replacement cost, relative to the
size, quality, and condition of the property. Compensation for other properties, including
tombs, brick or tile kilns, pump houses, wells, enclosures and lavatories will be
compensated by local governments in accordance with local practice, through direct
payments to property owners.
7.         The demolition of power and telecommunication lines and pipelines will also
be required. Compensation standards for such properties have been forinulted in
conjunction with utility agencies and will be paid direcdy to owners.
8.         In planning and budgeting for the highway ane RNIP resettlement programs,
a provision has been made for administrative cost, and a  ontingency (reserve) fund has
been established for unexpected costs within the approve preliminary budget and setting
out of the right-of-way (ROW).
C. PRNCPL   OF RESEFLEMENT
9.         The resettlement of farm workers affected by land acquisition involves
several alternatives to protect employment. First, "responsibility farmland will be
readjusted to provide cultivatable land to farmers.  Second, as mentioned above,
compensation fees held in the local development fund will be used to expand the
employment options available to farmers.
10.        In addition, township enterprises will be expanded to absorb surplus labor.
Employinent opportunities would be created in nearby state-owned enterprises for
transformation of agricultral households.
11.        The resettlement program will require residents to demolish and rebuild their
own houses. Factories, schools and hospitals will demoLsh and rebuild houses for their
staff; likewise, government institutions will resetle their own staff. Construction units of
the Fujian Provincial Expray Construction Directorate Office (FPECDO) will pay
compensation fees at replacement price for dwelling houses demoliton and relocation.
D.               PnocEDuI
12.        Investigation of Compensation Standards. FPECDO, in conjuncdon with
the Fujian Provincial Land Administation Bureau and the Fujian Provincial Transport
Planning and Design Institute (FPrPDI), completed a survey of the compesation standard
on land requisition and building relocation in early 1992. Data were collected on the total
area of farmland, population, types of crops, growing area, yield, crop prices, and value

of buildings. Based on these data, the average compensation values to be used in
estimating resettlement cost were formulated. Indicative compensation fees are shown
below:

E. RESEITLMrT FoR TE SIAMEN-QuOU  HiGHWAY
Route Location and Inpact
13.        The construction of the Xiamen-Quanzhou Hghway is the first phase of the
Province's longer-term objective of providing a high-standard highway in the well-
developed coastal corridor of the Province, lining the major cities of Zhangzhou-Xlamen-
Quanzhou and Fuzhou. The proposed highway section begins at Xifu near Km 185 on the
existing Fuzhou-Xiamen Highway, a point 10 km northeast of the center of Quanzhou
City. The section terminates at Guanlintou Village in Xinglin District, about 9 km
northwest of the center of Xiamen City. The length of the entire alignment is 81.4 km.
14.        The proposed route was chosen to minimize the acquisition of cultivated land
and the resetdement of residents. The land acquisiton and resettement activities for the
proosed highway will directly affect six counties and cities, with 18 towns and 1 farm.
A total of 9,565 mu of land will be acquired, and an additional 1,662 mu of land will be
occupied on a temporary basis. The cultivated land to be acquired for consructior. of the
highway totals 8,607 mu, or approxmately 1.6 percent of the total cultivated land in the
towns that are directly affected by resettement.
15.        The economic base of the communities along the highway alignment has
become increasingly diversified, due to the rapid growth of enterprises in recent years.
While agricultural activities have a cental role in the economy, the popuon affected by
resetdtement for the highway is active in a variety of sectors. Of the 15,504 people
affected by rsettlement under the highway project, approximately 31 pent are engaged
exclusively in farming, while 39 percent earn income from farming plus industry. About
S peicent are employed by enterprises or institutions, and the remaining 25 percent are
economically inactive. The impact of resettement on prpertie suggests that 84 percent
of the individuals would be affected by land acquisition, 8 percent would be affected by
demolition of houses, 6 percent would be affected by both land acquisition and demolition
of houses, and 2 percent would be affected only indirecdy.

Orgwitliondal Arrangements
17.        Organiztions for land requisition and resettlement were established between
April and October 1992. Leading groups have also been established at various levels in
the Province to involve representatives of planning, land administration, construction,
communications, labor, agriculture, water, electric power, post, and broadcasting
departments in the resetdement process.
18.        Provincial Level. Three staff members of the FPECDO will be broadly
responsible for implementation of the RAP. The agency's specific tasks include setting out
the ROW and verifying the quantity of land and strutures to be affected by resettement.
During implementation, the agency would make the preliminary budgetary allocations to
cities and counties for resettlement by contract, manage the inventory of land acquired for
the ROW, and monitor and audit the activities of lower-level implementing agencies.
19.        City Level. Resettlement offices at city levels will each be staffed by
10 people. The city-level offices will be responsible for carrying out the progr2m of
resettlement defined by the Directorate Office. The works concerning land acquisition and
resettlement in the area under each city's jurisdiction will form the basis of their work.
Other activities caried out at the city level will include resolution of civil disputes and
facilitation of contract site preparation, for example in acquisition or borrowing of pits and
quarries and the establishment of temporary power, water, and road systems.
20.         County Level. Offices of expressway construcdon at county levels will
have a total of 30 staff, representing 3 to S staff in each office. The county-level offices
would play a large role in verifying the amount of land acquired and buildings relocated
and allocating compensation fees to townships.
21.         Township mnd Viage Levels. Township agencies represent the working
level in implementation of the RAP, as most details of resetdement will be aranged and
supervised at township and village levels. A total of 36 people will coordinate resettement
activities at the township level, including 2 people per towraship. In addition, one person
wil handle compensation and land acquisition acdvities in each. village directly affected.
I



- 141 -                        ANN    6
22.         Survey of the ROW. The stakeout of the ROW was carried out by staff
of the FPTPDI between November 1992 and March 1993. Required approvals and other
formalities were also obtained or completed by the end of March 1993.
23.         Contracts. The agreements authorizing land acquisition have been signed
between FPECDO and the various local governments and land bureaus. Compensation
fees for demolition of buildings and acquisition of land to rebuild houses were paid to city
and county governments under lump-sum contracts, followed by contracting with lower-
level governments, during April 1993.
24.         Completion of ROW  Acquisition and Resettlement.  The structures
located within the ROW are scheduled to be demolished and removed between April and
October 1993. Properties will be removed by owners in principle, while resettlement
organizations will remove properties lackdng ownership. Land distribution was scheduled
for June 1993. Compensation will be paid after the demolition of buildings, and
resettlement of the population should be completed by the end of October 1993. An
inspection of the areas involved will follow these activities, with the goal of gaining access
to the ROW for construction by December 1993.
F. RESE lM   FOR TEIE ROAD NErwonK ImPmovzmr PROGRAM
25.         The land acquisition and resettlement activities for the RNIP, required only
for the "A" group of subprojects, will directly affect 12 towns or townships. A total of
1,928 mu of land will be acquired, and 20,085 e2 of buildings will be demolished. The
total number of people affected is 689.
26.         Resettlement for the RNEP will follow the general pnnciples staed above for
the highway.
27.         The compensation standards assumed for the RNIP vary by subproject, as
summarized below:
Land, including
Houses         compensation for craops

Nakou-Shaowu (A3)              165                 7,500
28.         In cases where houses must be demolished, township governments will
assign land for the construction of new houses. Cultivated land will be compensated
through the provision of newly reclaimed land, cash, or by employment with the
government, and resettlement will be provided to appropriate sites for those who wish to
continue farming. In the case of land acquisition or house demolition, people will be
prvided jobs in township- or village-based enteprises or in nearby industial companies.



- 142 -                       ANNE
29.         Organizational arrangements for RNIP resettlement activities provide for
coordination and supervision by FPHAB and the Fujian Land Administration Bureau. The
two agencies will jointly administer land acquisition, building demolition, and resettlement
of the population affected. The local agencies involved are located in suburban Fuzhou,
Lianjing county, Sanyuan District of Sanming, and Shaowu.
30.        The resettlement activities associated with RNIP are on schedule and will
likely be completed by the end of 1993. The establishment of local units to carry out
resettlement of RNIP took place in July 1993. The process of determining compensation
levels and contract amounts was completed by late August 1993, with assignment of land
and compensation payments made in September 1993. Removal of buildings and
assumption of land by contractors could be accomplished as early as November 1993, to
permit construction to begin in December 1993.
G. MONrrORING
31.        The implementation of the RAP for the highway will be monitored by
FPECDO. Each agency responsible for executing the RAP will moitor progress on a
continuous basis, through collection of data, interviews, and on-site spot checks of
resettlement activities. FPECDO plans to conduct a sample survey at the village level
early in the process of RAP implementation, to review compensation received by
individuals and the effect on incomes. FPECDO staff will also be involved in random spot
checks and interviewing at local levels to monitor resettlement. Readjustment of land and
employment will be monitored periodically, as frequently as results permit.
32.        FPHAB will be responsible for monitoring progress in resetement under
the RNIP. As with the highway, a formal process of progress reporting and review will
be used for each RNIP subproject, complemented by spot checks at resettlement sites and
by interviews with the population affected.
33.        It has been discussed and agreed that a report would be submitted to the
Bank in September 1994, reviewing the completed resettlement programs for the highway
and RNIP.
H. SUNMARE
34.        The estimated total cost of resetlement under the proposed project is
Y 141.4 million. A total of 16,193 people will be direcdy affected by resettlement
activities. A set of data related to the impact of resettlement for the proposed highway,
including number of people affected, amount of land to be acquired, and a summary of
resettlement costs, are provided in Appendixes 1 and 2. Similar data for the RNIP are
included in Appendixes 3 and 4.

TOLL RATE STUDY FOR                      -QUANZHOU UGHWAY
OUTI TERMS OF REFERENCE
Objective of Stud'
1.         The objective of the study is to analyze and recommend a toll rate structure
for the Xiamen-Quanzhou Highway. The study is expected to give proper consideration
to cost recovery goals, economic efficiency and equity in the toll strucure among different
classs of vehicles.
Prciples and Data for s*abin Toll Rates
2.         Pricing the use of roads should ta  into account cost recovery objectives,
economic efficiency and equity among users. Achieving a proper balance among these
objectives will be influenced by the level and composition of trffic, its effect on the cost
of opeang and maintaining the road, the vehicle operating costs on the Highway, the
existnce of alternative routes and the vehicle operating costs on such routes, including the
toll charges on such routes, if any, and the administrative cost of operating the toll
hfilities.
3.         While the toll revenue, in accordance with the present policies of the
Province, would be used primarily for the repayment of the loan, the analysis should also
eplore to what extent the operating and maintenance cost could also be coveted fom the
toll revenues. For this purpose, the study should come up with a realistic estimate of the
opeating and maintenance cost of the highway over at least a 20-year horizon. The
analysis should take into account the existence of route alternatives, and the difference in
vehicle operating costs, including the toll charged at the tolling stations, between the new
and the existing road, which will influence the vehicle driver's decision to use the new toll
Highway or to remain on the old toll road. For example, the traffic, discouraged by the
tolls on the new road, may remain on the lower-quality existing roads and incur higher
vehicle opting costs. Such higher costs represent an economic loss for the society. Toll
levels should be set to minimiz such losses to the regional and national economy.
4.          In order to be able to set a toll rate structure compatible with the above
principles, the following essential data will be required:
(a)   traffic composition on the existing road, both existing and projected, under
tolling situation, and with breakdown by origin and destinafton;
(b)  identification of alternative routes for the various origin-destnation pairs;



- 151-                         ANNEX I
(c)   vehicle operating costs on the highway and on the alternative routes,
including the costs on access roads to and from the highway;
(d)  in light of (a) through (c), estimates of traffic demand elasticity to toll
prices; and
(e)   vehicle types, and their relative costs imposed on road maintenance.
Ton Revenue and Traffc Diversion Projections
5.          On the basis of the proposed toll rate structure for the Highway, and the
present and projected traffic and tolling costs data, the study will make estimates of:
(a)   total toll revenue (from the Highway) to be collected yearly, over a period
of 20 years;
(b)   net toll revenue (from the Highway), on a yearly basis, once toll collection
costs are taken into account; and
(c)   estimates of the traffic that would not use the Highway as a result of the toll
charges.
Consideration of Chinese Experience withb Toll Roads
6.          The study will take into account the experiences to date with toll roads in
China, especially those under conditions similar to the Xiamen-Quanzhou highway. These
exeiences will be especially useful for determining the data on vehicle operating costs,
taffic demand elasticities and road maintenance costs. The review of the Chinese
experiences should look particularly at the level of toll rates charged, their relation to
veicle operating costs savings and drivers' behaviors due to the toll between the new and
the eisting routes, and the extent of traffic diversion.
Completion of the Study
7.          The study is expected to be completed and submitted to the World Bank for
comments by July 31, 1997.
